  What's notable about the wording:

  doesn't point the user to any of it.

   ‚ÄĒ it's a pattern.
  - Compared to SELECT (which says "Study each planning source. Study each spec
  doc that exists. Stop and review..."), DRAFT is quite terse.

  What are you thinking about changing here?

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 3 files (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Now I have a clear picture. Here's what the references say the architect
  should be doing during DRAFT, compared to what the forgectl output actually
  tells them:

  What the skill/references prescribe for drafting (from spec-format.md "Quick 
  Reference" and spec-generation-skill.md):

  1. Write the Topic of Concern (one sentence, no "and")
  2. Define the Interface ‚ÄĒ inputs, outputs, rejection
  3. Write Behaviors ‚ÄĒ preconditions, steps, postconditions, error handling;
  declarative voice
  4. Identify Invariants ‚ÄĒ always-true properties
  5. Decide Edge Cases ‚ÄĒ scenario, expected behavior, rationale
  6. Write Testing Criteria ‚ÄĒ Given/When/Then for every behavior, invariant,
  edge case
  7. Add Configuration and Observability if applicable
  8. Check for open questions (none allowed)
  9. List what the spec Implements
  10. Split if the topic is too broad (topic-of-concern test)

  What forgectl currently says at DRAFT:

  Action:  Draft all specs that need to be created or updated in the batch.
           After completion of the above, advance to begin evaluation.

  That's it ‚ÄĒ two lines. The entire spec-writing methodology is invisible to the
   user. The skill prompt knows all this, but if someone is using forgectl
  without the skill (or with a different skill), they get no guidance.

  What we could add to the DRAFT action output:

  The action block could include a concise checklist that mirrors the drafting
  workflow ‚ÄĒ not the full reference docs, but enough to remind the architect of
  the key steps and constraints:

  Action:  Draft all specs in the batch. For each spec:
           1. Write the Topic of Concern ‚ÄĒ one sentence, no "and".
           2. Define Interface ‚ÄĒ inputs, outputs, rejection conditions.
           3. Write Behaviors ‚ÄĒ preconditions, steps, postconditions, error
  handling.
              Use declarative voice ("the system does", not "the system
  should").
           4. Identify Invariants ‚ÄĒ always-true properties, each must be
  testable.
           5. Decide Edge Cases ‚ÄĒ scenario, expected behavior, rationale.
           6. Write Testing Criteria ‚ÄĒ Given/When/Then for every behavior and
  invariant.
           7. Add Configuration and Observability sections if applicable.
           8. Verify: no open questions, no planning file paths, no
  "should/could/might".
           If a topic is too broad, split into multiple spec files.
           After completion of the above, advance to begin evaluation.

  This keeps the output self-contained ‚ÄĒ the forgectl scaffold becomes useful
  even without the skill context. It also aligns with the common eval findings
  (missing observability, untested invariants, vague voice) by surfacing those
  reminders before the draft rather than catching them after.

  Want me to update the spec with this revised DRAFT output?

‚ĚĮ Instead, can you add references to the skill files that the user of Forgectl

  The rationale:

  - spec-format.md ‚ÄĒ the structure and section order. This is the "what does a
  spec file look like" reference.
  - spec-generation-skill.md ‚ÄĒ the drafting process, constraints, anti-patterns,
   and common eval findings. This is the "how do I write one well" reference.
  - topic-of-concern.md ‚ÄĒ the scoping test. This is the "do I need to split
  this" reference.

  These three cover the full drafting workflow without duplicating their content
   into the output. If the guidance evolves, it evolves in those files ‚ÄĒ the
  forgectl output just points to them.

  Open questions for you:

  1. Should these be absolute paths or relative paths? The skill references use
  relative paths like references/spec-format.md. Forgectl would need to know
  where these live ‚ÄĒ are they bundled with the project (in .forgectl/ or
  similar), or are they skill-specific files that only exist in the Claude skill
   context?

  report and address any findings." It could additionally point to the same
  format/process references since the architect is revising the draft.
  3. Is the three-reference set right, or would you add/remove any?

‚Źļ Okay, now I have the full picture. Here's what status currently outputs and
  why it's too much:

  The problem: status dumps everything ‚ÄĒ the current action, the queue, the
  completed history with every eval round, and (in implementing) every single
  item in every layer. The user's example had 18 items listed individually.
  That's useful for auditing but overwhelming for "what do I do next?"

  What I think status actually needs to answer:

  1. Where am I? ‚ÄĒ phase, state, round
  2. What do I do? ‚ÄĒ the action block
  3. How far along? ‚ÄĒ progress summary (not item-by-item)

  Proposed simplified status:

  Session: forgectl-state.json
  Phase:   implementing
  State:   IMPLEMENT
  Config:  batch=2, rounds=1-3, guided=true

  Item:    [daemon.io] PID file I/O operations (2 of 2)
  Layer:   L1 Core (2/5 layers)
  Round:   0

  Action:  Implement this item.
           After completion of the above, advance to continue.

  Progress: 3/18 passed, 0 failed, 15 remaining

  What gets cut:

  - --- Specifying --- / --- Planning --- sections ‚ÄĒ past phase history. You
  already went through those phases; their eval round details aren't actionable
  anymore.
  - Item-by-item listing in Implementing ‚ÄĒ replaced by a one-line progress
  summary. The full breakdown is in the state file if you need it.
  - Queue listing ‚ÄĒ the queue is in the state file. Status just needs to tell
  you what's current.
  - Per-item eval history in Completed ‚ÄĒ "2 rounds" is enough; you don't need
  the round-by-round paths in the status output.

  For specifying, same idea:

  Session: forgectl-state.json
  Phase:   specifying
  State:   REFINE
  Config:  batch=3, rounds=1-3, guided=true

  Batch:   Repository Loading, Snapshot Diffing, Cache Invalidation (optimizer)
  Round:   1/3

  Action:  Read the eval report and address any findings in the spec files
           using the spec skill.
           Eval report: optimizer/specs/.eval/batch-1-r1.md
           Format:      references/spec-format.md
           Process:     references/spec-generation-skill.md
           Scoping:     references/topic-of-concern.md
           After completion of the above, advance to continue evaluation.

  Progress: 1/5 specs completed, 2 queued

  The question is: do you want a --verbose flag that shows the full breakdown
  (what status does today), or is that unnecessary since the state file itself
  has all the detail?

  ‚Ēā plan-queue.json     ‚Ēā planning              ‚Ēā at init or phase shift     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā plan.json           ‚Ēā planning/implementing ‚Ēā at VALIDATE state and      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                     ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā phase shift                ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā forgectl-state.json ‚Ēā all                   ‚Ēā on every command (read)    ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  So there are three user-facing input files and one internal file. The question
   is whether --phase is the right axis. Looking at this:

  - forgectl validate --phase specifying spec-queue.json ‚ÄĒ validates spec queue
  - forgectl validate --phase planning plan-queue.json ‚ÄĒ validates plan queue
  - forgectl validate --phase implementing plan.json ‚ÄĒ validates plan.json (with
   the 12 checks)

  But plan.json is also validated during the planning phase (VALIDATE state runs
   the same 12 checks). So --phase creates ambiguity: does --phase planning mean
   "validate a plan queue" or "validate a plan.json"?

  Alternative: infer the file type from the content or use explicit subcommands:

  Option A ‚ÄĒ infer from content:
  forgectl validate <file_path>
  Peek at the top-level key ("specs" ‚Üí spec queue, "plans" ‚Üí plan queue,
  "context" + "layers" + "items" ‚Üí plan.json) and run the right validation. No
  --phase flag needed.

  Option B ‚ÄĒ explicit type flag:
  forgectl validate --type spec-queue <file_path>
  forgectl validate --type plan-queue <file_path>
  forgectl validate --type plan <file_path>

  Option C ‚ÄĒ your original proposal, but phase maps to the input file for that
  phase:
  forgectl validate --phase specifying <file_path>   # spec-queue
  forgectl validate --phase planning <file_path>     # plan-queue
  forgectl validate --phase implementing <file_path> # plan.json

  I'd lean toward Option A (auto-detect from content) since the three JSON
  formats have distinct top-level keys and it's the simplest UX. --phase could
  be an optional override for edge cases. What do you think?

‚Źļ Good. Now for the logging discussion ‚ÄĒ let me check what commands and states
  currently exist to map out what should be logged.

‚Źļ Explore(Research forgectl commands for logging)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Done (18 tool uses ¬∑ 68.3k tokens ¬∑ 41s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Here's what the research shows for logging:

  Commands that mutate state (should log):
  - init ‚ÄĒ session created
  - advance ‚ÄĒ every state transition, verdicts, round increments, forced
  acceptances, batch/item selections

  Read-only commands (skip):
  - status, eval, --version, validate

  So your instinct was right ‚ÄĒ advance is the main one, plus init. eval is
  read-only (it assembles context for sub-agents but doesn't change state),
  so it doesn't need logging.

  For the JSONL format, here's what I'm thinking each entry looks like:

  {"ts":"2026-03-29T14:32:01Z","cmd":"init","phase":"specifying","state":"ORIENT
  ","detail":{"from":"spec-queue.json","batch_size":3,"rounds":"1-3","guided":tr
  ue}}
  {"ts":"2026-03-29T14:33:12Z","cmd":"advance","phase":"specifying","prev_state"
  :"ORIENT","state":"SELECT","detail":{"batch":["repository-loading","snapshot-d
  iffing","cache-invalidation"],"domain":"optimizer"}}
  {"ts":"2026-03-29T14:45:00Z","cmd":"advance","phase":"specifying","prev_state"
  :"SELECT","state":"DRAFT","detail":{}}
  {"ts":"2026-03-29T15:10:33Z","cmd":"advance","phase":"specifying","prev_state"
  :"DRAFT","state":"EVALUATE","detail":{"round":1}}
  {"ts":"2026-03-29T15:12:01Z","cmd":"advance","phase":"specifying","prev_state"
  :"EVALUATE","state":"REFINE","detail":{"round":1,"verdict":"FAIL","eval_report
  ":"optimizer/specs/.eval/batch-1-r1.md"}}

‚Źļ 1. Session identity

  The state file doesn't have a session ID today. We'd need to add one. Options:

  - UUID v4 ‚ÄĒ random, globally unique, no collision risk. "session_id": 
  "a3f1b2c4-...". Simple but opaque.
  - ULID ‚ÄĒ sortable by time, still unique. "session_id": "01HYQX...". Nice for
  log file sorting.
  - Composite ‚ÄĒ <domain>-<phase>-<date>-<short-random>, e.g.,
  optimizer-specifying-20260329-a3f1. Human-readable in filenames.

  I'd lean toward UUID v4 in the state file (it's the Go standard ‚ÄĒ google/uuid
  is already common), but use it to name the log file with a human prefix:

  ~/.forgectl/logs/optimizer-specifying-a3f1b2c4.jsonl

  The session_id gets set once at init and never changes. It's written into
  forgectl-state.json at the root level. Archived sessions keep it. The log
  filename uses it so you can correlate logs to state files.

  Does that work, or do you want pure UUID filenames?

  ---
  2. ORIENT state ingestion

  What I meant: in the implementing phase, when advance transitions to ORIENT,
  the scaffold reads plan.json to calculate the next batch ‚ÄĒ it scans items,
  checks which are unblocked, selects up to batch_size. This is the moment where
   the plan's current state (which items are pending/done/passed/failed) gets
  "ingested" to decide what happens next.

  The log entry for this would capture what was selected and why:

  {"ts":"...","cmd":"advance","phase":"implementing","prev_state":"COMMIT","stat
  e":"ORIENT","detail":{"layer":"L1","batch_items":["daemon.types","daemon.io"],
  "unblocked":2,"remaining":5}}

  In specifying, ORIENT does the same thing ‚ÄĒ pulls the next batch from the
  queue:

  {"ts":"...","cmd":"advance","phase":"specifying","prev_state":"ACCEPT","state"
  :"ORIENT","detail":{"domain":"portal","batch":["portal-rendering","portal-cach
  ing"],"queue_remaining":0}}

  This is just a normal advance log entry with richer detail when the target
  state is ORIENT. Not a separate mechanism ‚ÄĒ just making sure we capture the
  batch selection context in the log.

  ---

  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  How they interact:
  - Both retention_days and max_files apply ‚ÄĒ whichever triggers first. A
  session from 10 days ago gets kept if you're under 50 files and under 90 days.
  - Pruning runs at init time (once per session start, not on every advance).
  - When enabled: false, no log file is created and no pruning runs.

  What I'd skip:
  - Max file size ‚ÄĒ JSONL entries are tiny (~200 bytes each), and sessions are
  bounded by the number of items in the queue. A 50-item implementing session
  might produce ~200 log lines. Size-based rotation adds complexity for a
  problem that won't happen.
  - Compression ‚ÄĒ same reasoning. The files are small.

  Thoughts on these three? Too many knobs, or about right?

‚ĚĮ 1. Yes, UUID V4 sounds great.                                                 
2. sounds good                                                                  
3. awesome sounds great.  when does the pruning apply?                          
    - How do you know which file to delete first?                               
                                                                                

‚Źļ When pruning runs: at init only ‚ÄĒ once per session start. Not on every
  advance, not on status. This keeps it simple and predictable. You're starting
  a new session, so it's a natural moment to clean up old ones.

  Deletion order for max_files: by file creation time (oldest first). Since each
   log file is created at init, the file's creation timestamp is the session
  start time. We could also parse the first JSONL entry's ts field as a
  fallback, but filesystem creation time is simpler and sufficient.

  Deletion order for retention_days: same ‚ÄĒ any file whose creation time is
  older than now - retention_days gets deleted.

  So the pruning algorithm at init is:

  1. List all .jsonl files in ~/.forgectl/logs/
  2. Sort by creation time (oldest first)
  3. Delete any file older than retention_days (if retention_days > 0)
  4. If remaining file count exceeds max_files (and max_files > 0), delete
  oldest until at or below the limit
  5. Create the new session's log file

  One edge case worth deciding: do we delete a log file for a session that's 
  still active? If someone has two forgectl sessions in different directories
  and one is long-running, we shouldn't prune its log. We could check if a
  corresponding forgectl-state.json exists and isn't archived yet ‚ÄĒ but that
  adds complexity. Simpler approach: just don't prune the current directory's
  session. Since pruning runs at init before the new log file is created, and
  we're deleting by age/count, an active session in another directory would only
   be at risk if it's the oldest file and you've hit max_files. At 50 files
  default, this is unlikely.

  Want to keep it simple (no active-session check) or add that safeguard?

‚ĚĮ We will assume that we will never delete an active session. This is assumed,  
but I'll make a note in my meeting tomorrow about this.

‚Źļ Let me work through these one at a time.

  The confusion about phases:

  Here's the current flow and where the gap is:

  specifying (produces specs) ‚Üí COMPLETE ‚Üí PHASE_SHIFT ‚Üí planning (produces
  plan.json) ‚Üí PHASE_SHIFT ‚Üí implementing
                                                ‚ÜĎ
                                      requires --from plan-queue.json
                                      WHO CREATES THIS?

  The spec-queue.json has an equivalent story ‚ÄĒ it's created by a search step
  before forgectl init. But plan-queue.json is different because forgectl
  already has everything it needs to generate it at the end of specifying:
  completed specs grouped by domain, file paths, commit hashes.

  So I think what you were getting at is: forgectl should generate the 
  plan-queue.json automatically at the phase shift, rather than requiring the
  user to create it externally. The data is already in the state file.

  This isn't really a new phase ‚ÄĒ it's making the specifying‚Üíplanning phase
  shift smarter. Instead of advance --from plan-queue.json, the shift would
  produce the plan-queue from the completed specs list. The user might still
  need to provide code_search_roots per domain, but the rest (name, domain, file
   path, specs list) is derivable.

  Does that match what you were thinking? Or were you envisioning a separate
  interactive step where the user reviews/edits the plan-queue before it's
  consumed?

  On removing topic from plan-queue.json:

  Looking at the schema:
  {
    "name": "Service Configuration",
    "domain": "launcher",
    "topic": "...",          ‚Üź this one
    "file": "launcher/.forge_workspace/implementation_plan/plan.json",
    "specs": ["..."],
    "code_search_roots": ["..."]
  }

  I agree topic is redundant here. The planning phase is domain-scoped ‚ÄĒ one
  plan per domain. The "topic" is just "implement the specs for this domain."
  The specs themselves carry the topics. Removing it simplifies the schema and
  eliminates a field that's either duplicative or vague.

  On commit hashes in plan-queue.json:

  This makes sense ‚ÄĒ if the specifying phase tracked commit hashes against
  completed specs, those hashes tell the planning phase exactly what changed.
  The planning STUDY_SPECS step could then
  look at git diff <hash> to see the spec content as it was written, rather than
   just reading the current file.

  This connects back to the auto-generation idea: if forgectl builds the
  plan-queue at phase shift, it can pull commit_hashes from each completed spec
  and include them.

  So the plan-queue entry might look like:
  {
    "name": "Launcher Implementation Plan",
    "domain": "launcher",
    "file": "launcher/.forge_workspace/implementation_plan/plan.json",
    "specs": [
      {"file": "launcher/specs/session-init.md", "commits": ["7cede10",
  "8743b1d"]},
      {"file": "launcher/specs/state-persistence.md", "commits": ["a1b2c3d"]}
    ],
    "code_search_roots": ["launcher/"]
  }

  Or do you want the commits flat at the plan level rather than per-spec?

  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā specs        ‚Ēā completed[].file ‚ÄĒ all spec file paths,   ‚Ēā Yes         ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā              ‚Ēā grouped by domain                         ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā spec_commits ‚Ēā completed[].commit_hashes ‚ÄĒ flattened,    ‚Ēā Yes         ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā              ‚Ēā deduplicated                              ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā code_search_ ‚Ēā Not in state file. Forgectl doesn't know  ‚Ēā No          ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā roots        ‚Ēā where source code lives.                  ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā topic        ‚Ēā Removing this                             ‚Ēā N/A         ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  Verdict: Everything except code_search_roots can be auto-generated by
  forgectl. The user must provide the code search roots per domain.

  So the specifying‚Üíplanning phase shift could work like this:

  1. Forgectl auto-generates a plan-queue.json from completed specs (grouped by
  domain, with spec file paths and commit hashes)
  2. The user provides code_search_roots ‚ÄĒ either:
    - Option A: --from still required, but now it's a lightweight file with just
   domain‚Üícode_search_roots mappings that forgectl merges into the
  auto-generated queue
    - Option B: --roots flag per domain, e.g., --roots launcher=launcher/,lib/
    - Option C: code_search_roots is optional in plan-queue, defaults to
  ["<domain>/"] if not provided ‚ÄĒ the domain directory itself is the most common
   root

  My take: Option C is the simplest. Default code_search_roots to ["<domain>/"]
  and let the user override via --from if they need custom roots. This means the
   phase shift no longer requires --from ‚ÄĒ forgectl can generate the queue
  automatically, and --from becomes an optional override.

  The updated flow would be:

  specifying COMPLETE ‚Üí PHASE_SHIFT
    forgectl advance                           # auto-generates plan-queue from
  completed specs
    forgectl advance --from custom-queue.json  # OR user provides full override

  And the new plan-queue.json schema (removing topic, adding spec_commits):

  {
    "plans": [
      {
        "name": "Launcher Implementation Plan",
        "domain": "launcher",
        "file": "launcher/.forge_workspace/implementation_plan/plan.json",
        "specs": [
          "launcher/specs/session-init.md",
          "launcher/specs/state-persistence.md"
        ],
        "spec_commits": ["7cede10", "8743b1d", "a1b2c3d"],
        "code_search_roots": ["launcher/"]
      }
    ]
  }

  That's 5 fields instead of 6 (dropped topic, added spec_commits). spec_commits
   is the deduplicated list of all commit hashes from the completed specs in
  that domain.

  Does this direction feel right? Specifically:
  1. Auto-generate at phase shift with code_search_roots defaulting to
  ["<domain>/"]?
  2. --from as optional override rather than required?
  3. spec_commits as a flat list per plan entry (not per-spec)?

‚ĚĮ i think we need more work on this                                             
                                                                                
- It would seem that we need to add the ability to add more spec files during

‚Źļ Good questions. Let me think through the full flow.

  1. When to allow adding specs

  The architect discovers they need new specs at two natural moments:

  - During ACCEPT ‚ÄĒ they just finished drafting a batch and realized a topic
  needs splitting or a dependency is missing. They have deep context on the
  domain right now.
  - During DONE ‚ÄĒ all queued specs are complete, but before reconciliation, the
  architect reviews the full picture and spots gaps.

  I'd propose a forgectl add-queue-item command that's valid at these states.
  The action output at ACCEPT would mention it:

  State:   ACCEPT
  Phase:   specifying
  Domain:  optimizer
  Batch:   3 specs accepted
  Round:   2/3
  Action:  Batch accepted.
           If you identified additional specs needed, run:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --domain <domain> --topic
  <topic> --file <file> [--source <path>...]
           After completion of the above, advance to continue.

  And at DONE:

  State:   DONE
  Phase:   specifying
  Specs:   5 completed
  Action:  All individual specs complete.
           If you identified additional specs needed, run:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --domain <domain> --topic
  <topic> --file <file> [--source <path>...]
           Adding specs here re-enters ORIENT for the new items before
  reconciliation.
           When ready, advance to begin reconciliation.

  At DONE, adding a spec would re-enter ORIENT ‚Üí SELECT ‚Üí DRAFT ‚Üí ... for the
  new item. Once that's accepted (and its domain cross-referenced), the
  architect returns to DONE.

  2. Code search roots ‚ÄĒ collected per domain

  The architect knows where the code lives by the time they finish a domain's
  specs. The natural collection point is the domain completion boundary ‚ÄĒ
  specifically at CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW (or if user_review: false, at the
  transition out of CROSS_REFERENCE_EVAL).

  A command like:

  forgectl set-roots --domain <domain> <path> [<path>...]

  The CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW action output would prompt for it:

  State:   CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW
  Phase:   specifying
  Domain:  optimizer
  Round:   1/2
  Verdict: PASS

  Action:  Please review with your user.
           Set code search roots for this domain (used in planning phase):
             forgectl set-roots --domain optimizer optimizer/ lib/shared/
           After completion of the above, advance to continue.

  The roots get stored in the state file under
  specifying.domains["optimizer"].code_search_roots. If not set, defaults to
  ["<domain>/"] at phase shift.

  3. How specifying meshes into planning

  Here's the full revised flow:

  SPECIFYING PHASE
  ================
  For each domain:
    ORIENT ‚Üí SELECT ‚Üí DRAFT ‚Üí EVALUATE ‚áĄ REFINE ‚Üí ACCEPT
      ‚ÜĎ                                              ‚Ēā
      ‚Ēā  (add-queue-item adds specs here)            ‚Ēā
      ‚Ēā                                              ‚Ēā
      ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ more batches in domain? ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė
                      ‚Ēā no
                      ‚Ėľ
    CROSS_REFERENCE ‚Üí CROSS_REFERENCE_EVAL ‚Üí CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW
      (set-roots collected here)                     ‚Ēā
                                                     ‚Ēā
      ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ more domains? ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė
      ‚Ēā yes ‚Üí ORIENT (next domain)
      ‚Ēā no
      ‚Ėľ
    DONE
      (add-queue-item can re-enter ORIENT)
      ‚Ēā
      ‚Ėľ
    RECONCILE ‚Üí RECONCILE_EVAL ‚Üí RECONCILE_REVIEW ‚Üí COMPLETE

  PHASE_SHIFT (specifying ‚Üí planning)
  ====================================
    forgectl auto-generates plan-queue from:
      - completed specs grouped by domain
      - spec_commits from commit_hashes (deduplicated per domain)
      - code_search_roots from set-roots (or default to [<domain>/])
      - file path convention:
  <domain>/.forge_workspace/implementation_plan/plan.json
      - name convention: "<Domain> Implementation Plan"

    User runs:
      forgectl advance                          # auto-generate plan-queue
      forgectl advance --from custom-queue.json # OR full override

  PLANNING PHASE
  ==============
    (consumes plan-queue, produces plan.json per domain)

  What this means for the plan-queue.json schema:

  {
    "plans": [
      {
        "name": "Optimizer Implementation Plan",
        "domain": "optimizer",
        "file": "optimizer/.forge_workspace/implementation_plan/plan.json",
        "specs": [
          "optimizer/specs/repository-loading.md",
          "optimizer/specs/snapshot-diffing.md",
          "optimizer/specs/cache-invalidation.md"
        ],
        "spec_commits": ["7cede10", "8743b1d"],
        "code_search_roots": ["optimizer/", "lib/shared/"]
      }
    ]
  }

  5 fields: name, domain, file, specs, spec_commits, code_search_roots. Topic
  removed. All auto-derivable except code_search_roots which is collected during
   specifying or defaults to ["<domain>/"].

  Summary of new commands:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

‚ĚĮ - Would adqitem be more expressive somewhere else?                            

‚Źļ Yeah, let me reconsider. The question is: when does the architect actually
  discover they need a new spec?

  During REFINE ‚ÄĒ the eval sub-agent says "this spec is too broad, split it" or
  "this references behavior that isn't specified anywhere." The architect is
  actively fixing issues and might need to add a spec rather than patch the
  current one.

  During CROSS_REFERENCE ‚ÄĒ cross-referencing within the domain reveals a gap.
  "Spec A references an integration point with something that doesn't have a
  spec."

  During CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW ‚ÄĒ the architect is reviewing with the user and
  has the fullest picture of the domain. They naturally say "we're also missing
  X."

  During RECONCILE / RECONCILE_REVIEW ‚ÄĒ cross-domain reconciliation reveals
  gaps.

  ACCEPT is actually the weakest discovery point ‚ÄĒ by then the batch passed
  evaluation. If something was missing, the eval would have flagged it earlier.

  The strongest candidates are:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā         State          ‚Ēā                Why                ‚Ēā   Scope    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā REFINE                 ‚Ēā Eval told you to split or found a ‚Ēā Current    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                        ‚Ēā  gap                              ‚Ēā batch      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW ‚Ēā Fullest domain picture, already a ‚Ēā Current    ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                        ‚Ēā  user checkpoint                  ‚Ēā domain     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā RECONCILE_REVIEW       ‚Ēā Cross-domain gaps visible         ‚Ēā All        ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                        ‚Ēā                                   ‚Ēā domains    ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW stands out ‚ÄĒ it's already a user-facing pause, it's
  per-domain (so the context is fresh), and it's where we'd also collect
  set-roots. It becomes the domain checkpoint: review cross-refs, add missing
  specs, set code search roots.

  That would make CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW the single place where the architect
  prepares the domain for planning:

  State:   CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW
  Phase:   specifying
  Domain:  optimizer
  Round:   1/2
  Verdict: PASS

  Action:  Please review with your user.
           If additional specs are needed for this domain:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --domain optimizer --topic
  <topic> --file <file> [--source <path>...]
           Set code search roots for this domain (used in planning phase):
             forgectl set-roots --domain optimizer optimizer/ lib/shared/
           After completion of the above, advance to continue.

  Adding a spec here would re-enter ORIENT ‚Üí SELECT ‚Üí DRAFT ‚Üí ... for the new
  item, then return to CROSS_REFERENCE (since the domain now has a new spec to
  cross-reference).

  RECONCILE_REVIEW could also allow add-queue-item for cross-domain gaps
  discovered late.

  Does CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW (+ RECONCILE_REVIEW) feel like the right home?

‚úĽ Cogitated for 36s

‚ĚĮ ok, i'd like to consider DRAFT,  what do you think about that?                

‚Źļ DRAFT is actually the strongest choice. Here's why:

  The architect is in the material during DRAFT ‚ÄĒ reading planning sources,
  writing behaviors, defining interfaces. This is the exact moment they think:

  - "This topic is too broad, I need to split it"
  - "This spec depends on behavior that has no spec in the queue"
  - "The planning source describes something that deserves its own spec"

  By EVALUATE, they've already compromised ‚ÄĒ crammed too much into one spec or
  left a gap. Then the eval catches it, they go to REFINE, and now they're
  patching instead of making the right structural decision.

  DRAFT lets the architect act on the insight when it's fresh, before the eval
  has to tell them what they already knew.

  And it doesn't disrupt anything ‚ÄĒ add-queue-item just appends to the queue.
  The current batch continues. The new spec gets picked up in a future batch.

  The DRAFT action output would become:

  State:   DRAFT
  Phase:   specifying
  Domain:  optimizer
  Batch:   3 specs
  Specs:
    [1] repository-loading.md
        Sources: .forge_workspace/planning/optimizer/repo-snapshot-loading.md
    [2] snapshot-diffing.md
        Sources: .forge_workspace/planning/optimizer/snapshot-diffing.md
    [3] cache-invalidation.md
        Sources: .forge_workspace/planning/optimizer/cache-invalidation.md
  Action:  Draft all specs in the batch using the spec skill.
           Format:    references/spec-format.md
           Process:   references/spec-generation-skill.md
           Scoping:   references/topic-of-concern.md
           If a topic needs splitting or a missing spec is identified:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --domain <domain> --topic
  <topic> --file <file> [--source <path>...]
           After completion of the above, advance to begin evaluation.

  I'd still keep it available at CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW and RECONCILE_REVIEW too
   ‚ÄĒ those catch different types of gaps (domain-level and cross-domain). But
  DRAFT is the primary home.

  For set-roots, CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW still feels right ‚ÄĒ that's the domain
  completion checkpoint where the architect has finished all specs for the
  domain and knows the codebase.

  So the full picture:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā    Command     ‚Ēā            States             ‚Ēā     Discovery type     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§

  ---
  Conclusions

  add-queue-item ‚ÄĒ three tiers emerged:

  Tier: Primary
  States: DRAFT
  Rationale: Highest context + freshness + agency. The architect is creating
    information and discovering gaps in real time. This is where splitting
    decisions and missing-dep discoveries happen naturally. Zero flow disruption

    (appends to queue).
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Tier: Secondary
  States: CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW
  Rationale: Domain-complete checkpoint. Gaps visible at domain scope that
    weren't visible at batch scope. User is engaged. Natural review pause.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Tier: Tertiary
  States: RECONCILE_REVIEW
  Rationale: Cross-domain gaps. Costly (re-enters ORIENT, reruns cross-ref and
    reconcile for affected domain) but necessary as a safety net.

  REFINE scored close to DRAFT but loses on focus ‚ÄĒ the architect should be
  fixing eval findings, not making structural decisions. SELECT scored well on
  engagement but the architect hasn't created anything yet, so discoveries are
  premature.

  set-roots ‚ÄĒ clear winner:

  CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW is the only state where all conditions align: the
  domain is complete, the architect has full code knowledge for that domain, and
   the user is present. DONE works as a fallback but per-domain context has
  faded by then.

  Final recommendation:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 28 lines
      403  
      404  The scaffold does not read or write these files. This is a con
           vention for the architect and sub-agent. The eval sub-agent ev
           aluates all specs in the batch together in a single report.
      405  
      406 +### Add Queue Item                                            
      407 +                                                              
      408 +`forgectl add-queue-item` appends a spec to the end of the spe
          +cifying queue. It does not affect the current batch.          
      409 +                                                              
      410 +1. Validate the current phase is `specifying`.                
      411 +2. Validate the current state is DRAFT, CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW
          +, or DONE.                                                    
      412 +3. Validate all required flags: `--name`, `--domain`, `--topic
          +`, `--file`.                                                  
      413 +4. Validate `--name` is unique across both the queue and compl
          +eted specs.                                                   
      414 +5. Append the new entry to the end of `specifying.queue`.     
      415 +6. Write the state file.                                      
      416 +7. Print confirmation: spec name, domain, and queue position. 
      417 +                                                              
      418 +When `add-queue-item` is used at DONE and the queue was previo
          +usly empty, advancing from DONE re-enters ORIENT for the new i
          +tems. After those items complete (including their domain's cro
          +ss-reference), the scaffold returns to DONE. Reconciliation do
          +es not begin until the queue is empty again.                  
      419 +                                                              
      420 +### Set Roots                                                 
      421 +                                                              
      422 +`forgectl set-roots` stores code search roots for a domain. Th
          +ese roots are used during plan-queue generation at the specify
          +ing‚Üíplanning phase shift.                                     
      423 +                                                              
      424 +1. Validate the current phase is `specifying`.                
      425 +2. Validate the current state is CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW or DON
          +E.                                                            
      426 +3. Validate `--domain` matches a domain that has completed spe
          +cs.                                                           
      427 +4. Validate at least one positional path argument is provided.
      428 +5. Store the roots in `specifying.domains[<domain>].code_searc
          +h_roots`.                                                     
      429 +6. Write the state file.                                      
      430 +7. Print confirmation: domain and roots.                      
      431 +                                                              
      432 +Calling `set-roots` for a domain that already has roots overwr
          +ites the previous value.                                      
      433 +

      446  9. **Cross-reference scans all domain specs.** CROSS_REFERENCE
            discovers all `.md` files in `<domain_path>/specs/`, not just
            session specs.
      447  10. **User review fires once.** CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW is ente
           red at most once per domain (after the first CROSS_REFERENCE_E
           VAL), and only when `specifying.cross_reference.user_review` i
           s true.
      448  11. **User review overrides guided.** CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW f
           ires even when `config.general.user_guided` is false.
      449 +12. **add-queue-item is state-gated.** Only valid in DRAFT, CR
          +OSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW, or DONE within the specifying phase.    
      450 +13. **set-roots is state-gated.** Only valid in CROSS_REFERENC
          +E_REVIEW or DONE within the specifying phase.                 
      451 +14. **add-queue-item names are unique.** No duplicate names ac
          +ross queue and completed specs.                               
      452 +15. **DONE re-enters ORIENT when queue is non-empty.** If `add
          +-queue-item` populates the queue at DONE, advancing re-enters 
          +ORIENT instead of RECONCILE.

      487    - **Expected:** CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW (pause). Second round
            onward skips review.
      488    - **Rationale:** User review fires once per domain to involv
           e the stakeholder without blocking every round.
      489  
      490 +- **Scenario:** `add-queue-item` called during EVALUATE.      
      491 +  - **Expected:** Error: "add-queue-item is only valid in DRAF
          +T, CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW, or DONE states (current state: EVAL
          +UATE)." Exit code 1.                                          
      492 +  - **Rationale:** Queue modifications are restricted to state
          +s where the architect is the actor with sufficient context.   
      493 +                                                              
      494 +- **Scenario:** `add-queue-item` with a name that already exis
          +ts in the queue.                                              
      495 +  - **Expected:** Error: "spec name '<name>' already exists in
          + queue." Exit code 1.                                         
      496 +  - **Rationale:** Duplicate names create ambiguity in status 
          +output, depends_on references, and completed specs tracking.  
      497 +                                                              
      498 +- **Scenario:** `add-queue-item` called at DONE when queue is 
          +empty, then advance.                                          
      499 +  - **Expected:** Advance re-enters ORIENT. The new spec is pu
          +lled into a batch. After acceptance and cross-reference, retur
          +ns to DONE.                                                   
      500 +  - **Rationale:** DONE only advances to RECONCILE when the qu
          +eue is empty. Adding items re-opens the drafting loop.        
      501 +                                                              
      502 +- **Scenario:** `add-queue-item` called during DRAFT for a dif
          +ferent domain than the current batch.                         
      503 +  - **Expected:** Item appended to queue. Current batch contin
          +ues unaffected. The new item is processed when its domain come
          +s up in queue order.                                          
      504 +  - **Rationale:** Queue append does not disturb the current b
          +atch.                                                         
      505 +                                                              
      506 +- **Scenario:** `set-roots` called for a domain with no comple
          +ted specs.                                                    
      507 +  - **Expected:** Error: "domain '<domain>' has no completed s
          +pecs." Exit code 1.                                           
      508 +  - **Rationale:** Roots are collected for domains that have b
          +een specified. Setting roots for an unknown domain is likely a
          + typo.                                                        
      509 +                                                              
      510 +- **Scenario:** `set-roots` called twice for the same domain. 
      511 +  - **Expected:** Second call overwrites the first. No error. 
      512 +  - **Rationale:** The architect may refine their understandin
          +g of code locations.                                          
      513 +                                                              
      514 +- **Scenario:** Phase shift to planning with no `set-roots` ca
          +lled for a domain.                                            
      515 +  - **Expected:** `code_search_roots` defaults to `["<domain>/
          +"]` in the generated plan-queue entry.                        
      516 +  - **Rationale:** The domain directory itself is the most com
          +mon search root. Explicit roots override the default.         
      517 +

      672 +### set-roots stores roots per domain                         
      673 +- **Verifies:** Root storage in state file.                   
      674 +- **Given:** CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW, domain is optimizer.     
      675 +- **When:** `set-roots --domain optimizer optimizer/ lib/share
          +d/`                                                           
      676 +- **Then:** `specifying.domains["optimizer"].code_search_roots
          +` is `["optimizer/", "lib/shared/"]`.                         
      677 +                                                              
      678 +### set-roots rejected outside valid states                   
      679 +- **Verifies:** State gate enforcement.                       
      680 +- **Given:** DRAFT.                                           
      681 +- **When:** `set-roots --domain optimizer optimizer/`         
      682 +- **Then:** Exit code 1. Error names current state.           
      683 +                                                              
      684 +### set-roots overwrites previous value                       
      685 +- **Verifies:** Idempotent overwrite.                         
      686 +- **Given:** CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW. Domain optimizer already 
          +has roots `["optimizer/"]`.                                   
      687 +- **When:** `set-roots --domain optimizer optimizer/ lib/share
          +d/`                                                           
      688 +- **Then:** Roots updated to `["optimizer/", "lib/shared/"]`. 
      689 +                                                              
      690 +### set-roots rejects unknown domain                          
      691 +- **Verifies:** Domain must have completed specs.             
      692 +- **Given:** DONE. No completed specs for domain "unknown".   
      693 +- **When:** `set-roots --domain unknown unknown/`             
      694 +- **Then:** Exit code 1. Error names the domain.              
      695 +

  So we can make --domain optional with a default: if omitted, use the current
  domain from state. If provided, use the explicit value. Required only at DONE
  where there is no current domain.

  For set-roots this is clean ‚ÄĒ at CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW you're setting roots
  for the domain you just reviewed. At DONE you'd need to say which domain.

  For add-queue-item there's one wrinkle: at DRAFT, the architect might want to
  add a spec for a different domain than the current batch. The current spec
  already has an edge case for this ("add-queue-item called during DRAFT for a
  different domain than the current batch"). So --domain should still be
  available as an override, just not required when the current domain covers it.

  Proposed behavior:

  # At DRAFT or CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW ‚ÄĒ domain inferred
  forgectl add-queue-item --name "Cache Eviction" --topic "..." --file
  optimizer/specs/cache-eviction.md

  # At DONE, or cross-domain add ‚ÄĒ domain required
  forgectl add-queue-item --domain portal --name "Portal Auth" --topic "..."
  --file portal/specs/portal-auth.md

  # Error at DONE without --domain:
  # Error: --domain is required at DONE (no current domain). Exit code 1.

  Same pattern for set-roots:
  # At CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW ‚ÄĒ domain inferred
  forgectl set-roots optimizer/ lib/shared/

  # At DONE ‚ÄĒ domain required
  forgectl set-roots --domain optimizer optimizer/ lib/shared/

  Want me to update the spec with this optional-with-default approach?

  ‚éŅ ¬†Wrote 239 lines to forgectl/specs/validate-command.md
       1 # Validate Command
       2 
       3 ## Topic of Concern
       4 > The scaffold validates JSON input files against their expected
          schemas, with auto-detection from top-level keys.
       5 
       6 ## Context
       7 
       8 Forgectl consumes three types of JSON input files across its lif
         ecycle phases: spec queues, plan queues, and implementation plan
         s. Each has a distinct schema with specific validation rules. Th
         e `validate` command runs these validations independently of ses
         sion state ‚ÄĒ no active session is required.
       9 
      10 The command auto-detects the file type by inspecting the top-lev
         el JSON key. A `--type` flag allows explicit override when auto-
         detection is insufficient or when the user wants to be explicit.
     ‚Ä¶ +229 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Write(forgectl/specs/activity-logging.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Wrote 281 lines to forgectl/specs/activity-logging.md
       1 # Activity Logging
       2 
       3 ## Topic of Concern
       4 > The scaffold logs session activity to JSONL files in the user'
         s home directory for audit and debugging.
       5 
       6 ## Context
       7 
       8 Forgectl writes structured log entries to `~/.forgectl/logs/` in
          JSONL format. Each session gets its own log file, named with th
         e domain, phase, and session UUID. Logging captures state-mutati
         ng commands ‚ÄĒ `init`, `advance` ‚ÄĒ so the user can reconstruct
         what happened during a session.
       9 
      10 Read-only commands (`status`, `eval`, `validate`, `--version`) d
         o not produce log entries.

‚ĚĮ ok great,  Given what we have covered, were there any concerns that you had   
with the project or any caveats that we did not discuss? Do you have any        
questions or concerns? If this were to be in production, would anything likely  
fail? What are your thoughts?                                                   

‚Źļ Good question. Here are the things I'd flag:

  Inconsistencies we created but didn't resolve:

  1. RECONCILE_REVIEW doesn't exist. The state-persistence spec references it in
   status output examples, and we discussed adding add-queue-item there as a
  tertiary option. But spec-reconciliation's state machine has no
  RECONCILE_REVIEW ‚ÄĒ it goes RECONCILE_EVAL ‚Üí COMPLETE or RECONCILE_EVAL ‚Üí
  RECONCILE. This is a latent inconsistency across specs.
  2. Log file naming for multi-domain sessions. The activity-logging spec says
  files are named <domain>-<phase>-<session_id_prefix>.jsonl, but a specifying
  session processes multiple domains. Which domain goes in the filename? First
  domain in the queue? Not specified.

  Design gaps that could cause production issues:

  3. set-roots is unreachable when user_review: false. If
  specifying.cross_reference.user_review is false (the default),
  CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW is never entered. The only place to call set-roots is
  DONE, where per-domain context has faded. The default config creates a
  suboptimal UX for the primary collection point of code search roots. This
  means most users will rely on the auto-default of ["<domain>/"], which may be
  fine ‚ÄĒ but if they need custom roots, the experience is awkward.
  4. spec_commits will often be empty. Commit hashes are auto-registered at
  commit points when enable_commits is true, but if commits are disabled,
  spec_commits will be empty in the auto-generated plan-queue. The planning
  phase then has no spec diffs to reference. There's no warning or prompt
  about this during the phase shift. We might need the PHASE_SHIFT output to
  flag "Warning: 0 spec commits registered. Consider enabling commits before
  advancing."
  5. Active session pruning is unprotected. We documented the assumption that
  active sessions are never deleted, but the pruning algorithm has no mechanism
  to detect or skip active sessions. In practice this is low-risk (50 files
  default, sessions are short), but if someone runs many parallel sessions over
  time, the oldest active session's log could be pruned.

  Things that would fail under edge pressure:

  6. add-queue-item at DONE for a new domain. The architect adds a spec for a
  domain that was never in the original queue. After ORIENT ‚Üí SELECT ‚Üí DRAFT ‚Üí
  EVALUATE ‚Üí ACCEPT, it needs CROSS_REFERENCE. But the cross-reference scans
  <domain_path>/specs/ ‚ÄĒ what's the domain_path for a domain that wasn't in the
  original queue? The spec-queue entries have domain_path but add-queue-item
  doesn't have a --domain-path flag. It only has --domain and --file. The
  scaffold would need to derive domain_path from the --file path or require it
  explicitly.
  7. Auto-generated plan-queue domain ordering. When auto-generating the
  plan-queue at phase shift, the spec says "group completed specs by domain" but
   doesn't specify what order the domains appear in. Queue order? Alphabetical?
  Completion order? This affects which domain gets planned first.

  Questions I'd want answered before shipping:

  8. Should set-roots also be available at DONE for the user_review: true case,
  or is CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW sufficient? (It is available at DONE, so this is
  covered ‚ÄĒ but the default config makes DONE the only option.)
  9. Should the PHASE_SHIFT output warn about missing spec commits, or is empty
  spec_commits an acceptable default?
  10. Do we need a --domain-path on add-queue-item, or can the scaffold derive
  it from the --file path (e.g., optimizer/specs/new-spec.md ‚Üí domain_path: 
  optimizer/)?

  Items 1, 3, 4, and 6 are the ones I'd want resolved before implementation. The
   rest are minor or have reasonable defaults.

‚úĽ Crunched for 52s

‚Źļ Let me address #6 first since you want discussion, then we'll tackle the spec
  changes.

  #6 ‚ÄĒ add-queue-item at DONE for a new domain: the domain_path problem

  Today, every spec in the queue has a domain_path that comes from the
  spec-queue.json input file. The scaffold uses it to:
  - Resolve full spec paths: <domain_path>/specs/<filename>
  - Discover all .md files in <domain_path>/specs/ for cross-referencing
  - Display shorter paths in output

  When the architect uses add-queue-item, they provide --file 
  optimizer/specs/new-spec.md. The scaffold needs to derive domain_path from
  that. Two options:

  Option A ‚ÄĒ Derive from --file:
  Parse the file path to extract the domain directory. If --file is
  optimizer/specs/new-spec.md, then domain_path is optimizer/. This works for
  the standard convention <domain>/specs/<name>.md but breaks if someone uses a
  non-standard path like libs/shared/specs/new-spec.md ‚ÄĒ is the domain libs/ or
  libs/shared/?

  Option B ‚ÄĒ Derive from --domain:
  The --domain flag already exists. If domain is optimizer, the scaffold assumes
   domain_path is optimizer/. This works because the convention is that the
  domain name is the top-level directory. The original spec-queue.json also
  follows this ‚ÄĒ domain and domain_path are almost always <domain>/.

  Option C ‚ÄĒ Match against known domains:
  When add-queue-item is called, the scaffold already has completed specs with
  domain_path values. If --domain optimizer is provided and we already have
  optimizer specs, we know the domain_path. If it's a brand new domain we've
  never seen, we fall back to <domain>/.

  I'd lean toward Option C with B as fallback: look up the domain in completed
  specs or existing queue entries to get the known domain_path. If the domain is
   entirely new, assume <domain>/. This handles the common case (adding to a
  domain we already know) and the rare case (adding a new domain) without
  requiring a new flag.

  The one risk: a brand new domain at DONE that uses a non-standard directory
  structure (e.g., domain is shared-utils but the directory is
  libs/shared-utils/). That's an edge case of an edge case. We could document
  that new domains added via add-queue-item assume <domain>/ as the domain path,
   and if that's wrong, use --from override at the phase shift.

  What do you think ‚ÄĒ is Option C sufficient, or do we need explicit
  --domain-path?

‚ĚĮ Can we add validation to the add queue item, please?  to verify that the file 
 exists                                                                         
walk me through the scenarios on this                                           

‚Źļ Sure. Here are the scenarios for validating the --file path on add-queue-item:

  Scenario 1 ‚ÄĒ File already exists (updating an existing spec)

  The architect is adding a spec that already has a file on disk ‚ÄĒ maybe from a
  previous session or written manually. The file at
  optimizer/specs/cache-eviction.md exists.

  - Validation: path exists, it's a .md file in a specs/ directory.
  - Result: passes. The scaffold can derive domain_path as optimizer/ from the
  path structure.
  - DRAFT/EVALUATE will work on this existing file.

  Scenario 2 ‚ÄĒ File doesn't exist yet (new spec to be drafted)

  The architect is adding a spec they haven't written yet.
  optimizer/specs/cache-eviction.md doesn't exist. This is the primary use case
  ‚ÄĒ the whole point of adding it to the queue is to draft it later.

  - If we require the file to exist: this fails. The architect can't add a spec
  they haven't written yet.
  - If we don't require it: passes, but we can't validate the path structure.

  Scenario 3 ‚ÄĒ Parent directory exists but file doesn't

  optimizer/specs/ exists as a directory, but cache-eviction.md doesn't. This is
   the happy path for new specs ‚ÄĒ the domain's specs directory is already set
  up.

  - We could validate that the parent directory exists instead of the file
  itself.
  - Result: confirms the domain path is real, the specs directory exists, the
  file just hasn't been written yet.

  Scenario 4 ‚ÄĒ Neither parent directory nor file exists

  brand-new-domain/specs/cache-eviction.md ‚ÄĒ neither the domain directory nor
  the specs directory exists. This is a brand new domain being added at DONE.

  - If we require parent directory: fails. But this might be legitimate ‚ÄĒ the
  architect is adding a spec for a domain that doesn't have any files yet.
  - If we just validate the path looks right (contains /specs/ and ends in .md):
   passes on structure, defers existence check.

  Scenario 5 ‚ÄĒ Typo in path

  optimzer/specs/cache-eviction.md ‚ÄĒ typo in domain name. No such directory
  exists.

  - This is what we'd want to catch.
  - Parent directory validation would catch this if the correct domain exists.

  My recommendation:

  Validate the parent directory exists, not the file itself. This catches typos
  (scenario 5) while allowing new specs (scenario 2-3). For brand new domains at
   DONE (scenario 4), we'd need to allow missing parent directories ‚ÄĒ or require
   the architect to mkdir -p first.

  The validation would be:
  1. Path ends in .md ‚ÄĒ it's a spec file
  2. Path contains /specs/ ‚ÄĒ it's in a specs directory
  3. Parent directory exists ‚ÄĒ the domain's specs directory is real
  4. Exception: if parent doesn't exist AND the domain is new (not in completed
  or queue), warn but allow ‚ÄĒ the architect is setting up a new domain

  Or simpler: validate parent directory exists, period. If the architect is
  adding a new domain, they create the directory first. That's a reasonable
  expectation.

  What's your preference ‚ÄĒ strict (parent must exist) or lenient (warn but
  allow)?

created the spec file and it needs to exist. Therefore, the architect must

  State: DONE

    work here since the architect would write it then. But that's what the
    original queue is for ‚ÄĒ not add-queue-item.

  The distinction is clear:

  - Queue (at init) = specs to be written. Files don't exist yet. That's the
  whole point of the specifying phase.
  - add-queue-item (mid-session) = specs already written that need to be tracked
   through evaluation. The architect created the file, now the scaffold needs to
   know about it.

  This is a fundamentally different intent. The original queue is a plan.
  add-queue-item is a registration of completed work.

  Validation rule: --file must point to an existing file. Error if not found:

  Error: file "optimizer/specs/cache-eviction.md" does not exist.
    add-queue-item registers specs that have already been written.
    Create the spec file first, then register it.

  And the action outputs should make this explicit. Updated wording:

  DRAFT:
           If a topic needs splitting or a missing spec is identified,
           write the new spec file, then register it:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --topic <topic> --file <file>
   [--source <path>...]

  CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW:
           If additional specs are needed for this domain,
           write the new spec file, then register it:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --topic <topic> --file <file>
   [--source <path>...]

  DONE:
           If additional specs are needed,
           write the new spec file, then register it:
             forgectl add-queue-item --name <name> --domain <domain> --topic
  <topic> --file <file> [--source <path>...]

  This also solves the domain_path problem from #6 ‚ÄĒ if the file exists at
  optimizer/specs/cache-eviction.md, the scaffold can derive domain_path from
  the file path. No guessing needed.

  Want me to update the specs with this?

‚Źļ Good, #2 is done. Now #3 ‚ÄĒ new state for set-roots when user_review is false
  and #1 ‚ÄĒ RECONCILE_REVIEW. Let me think about #3 first since it affects the
  spec-lifecycle state machine.

  The problem: when user_review: false, CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW is never entered,
   so the architect has no natural place to call set-roots per-domain except
  DONE. We need a new state that fires at the domain completion boundary
  regardless of user_review.

  This state should be specifically for collecting domain metadata (code search
  roots) before moving on. Let me read the current transition flow to find where
   it fits.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Here's my thinking on the new state. The cleanest approach: replace the
  (continue) decision point with a new state DOMAIN_COMPLETE that always fires
  when a domain's cross-reference passes. This state is where the architect
  calls set-roots and add-queue-item. CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW becomes part of
  DOMAIN_COMPLETE's behavior (when user_review: true, the output says "review
  with your user" in addition to the roots/queue-item instructions).

  Actually, simpler: just make the existing (continue) always go to
  CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW regardless of user_review. When user_review: false, the
   output just shows the set-roots and add-queue-item instructions without the
  "review with your user" line. This avoids adding a new state name ‚ÄĒ
  CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW becomes a mandatory domain checkpoint.

  Let me propose this to you before making changes:

  Current behavior:
  - user_review: true ‚Üí CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW (shows review + set-roots +
  add-queue-item)
  - user_review: false ‚Üí skip straight to ORIENT/DONE (set-roots only available
  at DONE)

  Proposed behavior:
  - CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW always fires once per domain (after first passing
  CROSS_REFERENCE_EVAL)
  - When user_review: true: output says "Please review with your user" +
  set-roots + add-queue-item
  - When user_review: false: output says just set-roots + add-queue-item (no
  user review prompt)

  This means:
  - user_review only controls whether the output includes "review with your
  user" ‚ÄĒ it no longer controls whether the state is entered
  - set-roots is always available at the domain boundary
  - No new state name needed
  - Invariant 10 ("User review fires once") becomes "CROSS_REFERENCE_REVIEW
  fires once per domain" regardless of user_review
  - Invariant 11 ("User review overrides guided") is no longer needed ‚ÄĒ the
  state always fires

  This is simpler than adding a new state. The trade-off is that user_review: 
  false sessions get one extra stop per domain, but it's a brief one ‚ÄĒ just run
  set-roots and advance. Does this direction work, or do you want a separate
  state name?

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 2m 44s

      193  ## Edge Cases
      194  
      195  - **Scenario:** Reconciliation eval finds no issues on first p
           ass, `specifying.reconciliation.min_rounds` is 0 (default).
      196 -  - **Expected:** RECONCILE ‚Üí RECONCILE_EVAL with `--verdict P
          -ASS` ‚Üí COMPLETE.                                              
      197 -  - **Rationale:** When `specifying.reconciliation.min_rounds`
          - is 0, a single PASS immediately completes. The happy path is 
          -a single round.                                               
      196 +  - **Expected:** RECONCILE ‚Üí RECONCILE_EVAL with `--verdict P
          +ASS` ‚Üí RECONCILE_REVIEW ‚Üí COMPLETE.                           
      197 +  - **Rationale:** When `specifying.reconciliation.min_rounds`
          + is 0, a single PASS triggers the review checkpoint, then comp
          +letes.

           et).
      201    - **Rationale:** Even with a passing verdict, minimum reconc
           iliation rounds must be completed when configured.

          -_rounds`.

          +_rounds`, round 1.

          +ut review checkpoint still fires on round 1).

          +point fires once for the architect to add late-discovered spec
          +s.

      205 -  - **Rationale:** The maximum reconciliation rounds are exhau

          + COMPLETE.

          +NE ‚Üí RECONCILE (reconciliation restarts).

      442  `forgectl add-queue-item` appends a spec to the end of the spe
           cifying queue. It does not affect the current batch.
      443

            with message instructing the architect to create the file fir
           st.

            `--domain` is required (no current domain).

            session specs.
